Rural Hygiene Work 191

— Editor

＝Pay Close Attention to the Health of Farmers＝

＝New Medicine and Pharmaceuticals Should Be Popularized to the Public＝

Rural hygiene work has two important meanings:

(1) We acknowledge that the most hardworking people in China today are the farmers, and also the poorest;

The lives lived by farmers in the Chinese interior are truly inhuman (perhaps they themselves are unaware): In terms of health, countless farmers with sallow faces and emaciated bodies continue to work like cattle and horses. A single outbreak of plague can kill many farmers, a single outbreak of smallpox can kill many small farmers. Even a minor illness forces them to seek out old-fashioned medicine, and countless souls are unjustly added to the City of the Dead. The deaths of women and infants during childbirth at the hands of old-style midwives are numerous. Alas, alas! As people who study new medicine and pharmaceuticals, can we sit idly by and watch our compatriots suffer and die unjustly? Arise! We must relieve their pain, we must prevent and treat their diseases, and we must find ways to improve their health so that farmers can live and work in peace. The restoration of agriculture is the most pressing issue of the day. To solve this problem relies entirely on the assistance of the government and the people, but a part of the responsibility rests on the shoulders of us in the field of new medicine. (2) When we recall that new medicine and pharmaceutical education has been practiced in China for a long time, the question is: who are the people who enjoy the benefits of new medicine and pharmaceuticals? The graduates of medical and pharmaceutical schools each year, those who return after studying abroad, are mostly in the cities. How can the poor villagers enjoy any of the benefits of new medicine? Because they do not enjoy the benefits of new medicine, they naturally do not believe in it. Everyone! Don't we want to make the entire country scientific in medicine and pharmaceuticals? Arise! Start in the villages. After ten years, scientific new medicine will likely be prevalent throughout the country, and unscientific old medicine will likely be completely eliminated?

Today, we raise this issue with two hopes: First, we hope that the entire field of new medicine and pharmaceuticals will, from today onwards, pay attention to this issue, contribute our implementation plans and opinions, and personally go to the villages and begin work.

Second, we hope that readers throughout the country will write to us about the health conditions in their hometowns and the areas they hope to improve. We will make them public to the masses at any time as a direction for research and improvement.

Discussion of Jiao Yitang's Letter to the Nation on the Adoption of National Medicine Regulations (Continued) 192

— Yu Yunxiu

Mr. Jiao said: "The shortcoming of national medicine is that in theoretical aspects, it is mixed with some metaphysics, and in comparison with modern science, there are naturally many places that do not match... Young national doctors, although they are learning national medicine, are very able to express abandonment of the metaphysical theories in national medicine, or at least hold a skeptical attitude because national medicine is empiricism and does not value theory. Generally, Western doctors believe that metaphysics is the basic consciousness of national medicine." Mr. Jiao is neither too tight nor too loose. I will tell you one thing: Experimentation requires the consciousness of material civilization, excellent equipment, and a mastery of natural sciences, mathematics, chemistry, and physics, and the examination must be precise. Only then can the results and records be detailed, avoid errors, approach the truth, and have true value in academics. If, as Mr. Jiao admits, material civilization is not advanced, there is no excellent equipment to use, and the national doctors' examination is imprecise, when exploring in terms of academic theory, what ability do they have to experiment? What tools do they use to experiment? What knowledge do they have to judge the phenomena obtained by experimentation? The Huainanzi Qisu Training says: "The Hu people see fake goods and do not know that they can be made into cloth. The Yue people see feathers and do not know that they can be made into felt. Therefore, it is difficult to talk about change with those who are not familiar with things." In the daily experience of noble national doctors, perhaps very valuable phenomena are occasionally revealed, but they are simply inexplicable, looking at them and thinking that they have grasped the essence. What further method is there? Mr. Jiao puts the word "experiment" in the hands of national doctors, which seems to be somewhat divorced from the scope of "exploring in terms of academic theory" and starting to make exaggerated publicity. Mr. Jiao, alas! The tricks that your noble national doctors are doing now can only be called "traditional habits." When a patient comes, they routinely take his pulse, routinely prescribe a prescription, use Ephedra for fever without sweat, use Pinellia for expectorant, use Poria for diuresis, use Aconite for weak pulse. In summer, they routinely use some fresh lotus leaves. If the patient gets better after taking the medicine, of course, it is my credit. If not, there is a large text of "Beware of changes" written at the end of the pulse record, and you can also say, "As I expected." Now, the parents in society generally worship and chant for the spirits, burn paper ingots, and take Xingjun Powder when their children are sick. They swallow Liushen Pills for a sore throat and scrape Sha for an upset stomach. The work of national doctors is exactly the same as these practices, completely inexplicable and following a routine story. Therefore, I say it is a "traditional habit." As for whether the pulse can diagnose the disease, whether Ephedra, Pinellia, Poria, Aconite, dried ginger, fresh lotus leaves, as well as worshipping, burning paper ingots, taking Xingjun Powder, swallowing Liushen Pills, and scraping Sha can cure the disease, whether the disease is cured because Ephedra, Pinellia, Poria, Aconite, dried ginger, fresh lotus leaves, and chanting work or for what reason can paper ingots, Xingjun Powder, Liushen Pills, Sha, etc. have effects and for what reason will Qin have effects, etc. they only look at it and do not understand at all. Therefore, the "traditional habits" worked by national doctors only provide some experimental materials to scientific doctors. If this is to be considered an experiment, this exaggerated publicity is a bit embarrassing.

Mr. Jiao hangs the sign of empiricism in front of the national medicine gate on the one hand, saying that they do not value theory, but on the other hand, he prepares for doctors to "explore from a theoretical perspective" and "study from a theoretical perspective." I don't know what the difference is between theory and learning in Mr. Jiao's mind?

"The possibility of science transformation, saying that it is science transformation, cannot be called national medicine. Regarding the latter point, academics can be consistent with science, but there can be different learning between countries." This is Mr. Jiao's mistake of comparing English, German, Japanese, and Chinese to English doctors, German doctors, Japanese doctors, and Chinese doctors. I have already clarified this in the first section of this discussion, so I will not say it again.

Mr. Jiao said: "In terms of experience,... although his diagnostic methods do not conform to science, they can conform to reality. Due to his diagnostic insights and treatment, although the theory is inaccurate, the efficacy is effective, just like three plus five plus eight. He can only tell you that the answer is ten, but he cannot create the formula. But curing diseases is not like researching other kinds of science. The requirement for the answer is more urgent than listing the formula." From these words, it seems that Mr. Jiao only understands elementary arithmetic. For simple problems like "three plus five plus eight," there is no need to list the formula. Mental arithmetic can be used to answer it. If you encounter advanced mathematics and physics, I am afraid that the formula is necessary! For superficial diagnoses, such as "Someone's wife has not had her period for more than a month, has a bit of a poor appetite, and often feels nauseous. She is pregnant." You don't need to ask your noble national doctors for this diagnosis. Even an illiterate village woman can tell you that. However, if there are problems with the uterus or ovaries, there are also the above-mentioned symptoms. In cases of doubt, it is necessary to determine whether she is pregnant or sick. At this time, or to prove whether or not she is pregnant, which affects legal and family matters, I am afraid that a complex formula is needed. Not only is the village woman useless, but also your noble national doctors' pulse principles, such as "One Yin beats Yang, meaning pregnancy," and "If a woman's hand Shaoyin pulse moves greatly, she is pregnant," are useless. When exploring this kind of answer in terms of academic theory, I am afraid that it is not as simple as "three plus five plus eight" and can be done with mental arithmetic. Therefore, mathematics that cannot produce a formula can only be considered a simple problem in elementary school and cannot be applied to advanced and complex science. This is what I said above: "Small paths are worth seeing, but going far is afraid of getting stuck, the gentleman does not do it."

Since Mr. Jiao knows that national doctors' diagnoses are not precise, and since he knows that even a formula cannot be created, then all the contradictory phenomena between theory and fact of your noble national doctors must also be attributed to the four words "luck and coincidence." In the past, old doctors with conscience and old doctors with research ideas also frankly said that it was luck. Zhang Huang, Wang Xunchen, Xu Lingtai, all of them. Only a group of city monks like your noble national doctors with the intention of deceiving people said that the effectiveness has been consistent. Mr. Jiao would also say "to grasp the essence," "to know why but not be able to tell others," and "his shortcoming is his strength," jumping out of the circle of academic exploration to talk nonsense. Mr. Jiao, alas! Experience is unreliable. Relying on experience without rigorously examining it with scientific experiments can easily lead to errors. In my "Critique of Huanghan Medicine," there is a passage on experience and experimentation that seems worth presenting to Mr. Jiao and the people of the country. I have excerpted it below for your humble reference!

"For example, on a tall building, if you throw a copper coin and a chicken feather at the same time, the copper coin will fall straight down, while the chicken feather will flutter and flutter and take a long time to reach the ground. The fact that the coin and feather fall at very different rates is something everyone feels. No one says it is wrong. It is absolutely true. I am afraid that there is no more reliable experience in the world than the fact that the coin and feather fall at different rates... But how could anyone know that when a scientist comes out and uses a long glass tube, puts the coin and feather in the tube, and evacuates the air inside, then inverting the tube, he can experiment and find that the coin and feather fall together, and it is not necessarily true that one is faster or slower. From this, a discovery is made: the phenomenon of an object falling is not only related to the object and the earth's gravity, but there is also a third party participating in the middle that is invisible and inaudible, which is the influence of air. This is something that the empiricist would never have dreamed of... Experience only knows the phenomenon that the coin is fast and the feather is slow. As for what third party is participating, what fourth party is mixed in, everything is unseen and unheard. Therefore, it is only enough to recognize a complex and mixed natural phenomenon. It cannot be analyzed to make further observations to understand the original appearance of the activities of each molecule to complete the detailed study of this phenomenon. In other words, it only knows the resultant force expressed in physics and cannot actually take a further step to analyze how its component forces are and where they come from. It only knows the ready-made compounds in chemistry and cannot actually take a further step to analyze how its molecules are and what method they are made of. Therefore, relying solely on experience will only use the ready-made things in nature and the things invented by human instincts. His ideas and theories can only be based on superficial and messy current phenomena to organize empty theories. He cannot follow the root and thoroughly make further research..."

People of the country! After reading this passage, you can know that experience alone is unreliable! National doctors say "experience" repeatedly, all taking the holistic phenomenon as a unit, taking the complex phenomena of luck and coincidence as simple and pure facts, as absolutely true effects, as clear and understandable strengths. When exploring in terms of academic theory, there is no value at all. Mr. Jiao really should not talk about that kind of thing.

The True Meaning of Pharmacy Business (4) 193

— Min

Pharmacies in Norway and Sweden

The pharmacy systems of the two countries are the same. All pharmacies are specialized vocational businesses, that is, in addition to formal pharmacies, so-called ordinary grocery stores are very few. Their formal pharmacies are called Apotek, similar to Germany, with complete content and brilliant appearance. Only pharmacists can sell medicines. In other words, pharmacies are all opened by pharmacists, so the number of pharmacies is strictly fixed. That is, when a store owner dies, causing the store to close or add a new quota, the public must be notified first, and then the government selects qualified pharmacists. The recording of other public officials is the same, and they must also examine profound knowledge and pharmaceutical skills before they are allowed to replace or open a store. The daily business hours of the pharmacy are 12 hours, that is, from 8 or 9 am to 7 or 8 pm, and for the convenience of customers, the city's pharmacies are divided into several groups so that they can be on duty on Sundays, holidays, and nights throughout the year. Most pharmacies also hire qualified female assistants to practice in them. These assistants are dressed in white, which seems to match their professional attitude and capable skills. Therefore, the cleanliness and tidiness of their pharmacies are not without reason. Also, their pharmacists do not work in laboratories such as analytical and microscopic examinations, which is the same as in Belgium, but different from pharmacies elsewhere in Europe. Because there are other specialized agencies in society to handle these tasks.

The pharmacy business in the above-mentioned countries can represent the pharmacy industry system in the entire Europe. Although the pharmacy business in some countries may not be exactly the same, the business purpose of their formal pharmacies is the same. It is nothing more than using specialized occupations to give full play to their skill contributions, which is a correct and grand purpose to serve human society. It is different from ordinary stores. As for the cultivation of morality, although it is ruled by national law, and when we trace the source, it is attributed to pharmaceutical education a lot (The End).

A Bird's-Eye View of Shanghai's Medical and Pharmaceutical Scene Over the Past Decade (Continued) 194

— Kuo Ching-chou

Chapter VI: Medical and Pharmaceutical Education and Publications

Section 1: New Medical and Pharmaceutical Education

Nurses are crucial in modern medicine and pharmacy and should ideally have their own specialized departments with intensive training. However, in Shanghai, past nurses were trained independently by hospital-affiliated nursing programs. There was no standardized skill requirement, and while the work-study format of these programs benefited both students and hospitals, the inconsistent admission standards and inadequate instruction often led to uneven results. Moreover, hospitals varied in size and curriculum, and the languages studied included English, Japanese, German, and French. Additionally, midwifery school graduates, feeling they were taking a step down, reluctantly became nurses (though their training might not have suited them). Even clinics calling themselves hospitals liberally issued nursing diplomas. As a result, the nursing profession became a mixed bag, with varying levels of competence; some were audacious enough to become quack doctors, while others were too weak to find a place for themselves. Currently, Shanghai has two special nurses' associations, which temporarily meet the needs of patients and doctors, acting as employment agencies. I sincerely hope these two associations will develop in the future and, together with enthusiastic medical officials, work to organize the nursing profession in Shanghai.

Besides schools, there are also specialized research institutes, intended for graduated physicians and pharmacists to further their knowledge of fundamental medical and pharmaceutical sciences, not for ordinary students. However, the achievements in these institutes are, after all, the roots of academic theory, so I will briefly list them here.

Research institutions can be divided into two categories: the first being the research laboratories within schools. Besides providing students with practical experience, they naturally also provide professors and assistants in each department with opportunities for advanced research. Given the current economic conditions of various schools, these school research labs are not yet fully developed. Now, speaking only of independent research institutes, there are the following few, but unfortunately, not all are run solely by Chinese, and the range of subjects is not yet extensive enough.

(1) The Lister Institute: Founded with funds from the Englishman Lister, its new building on Avenue Road was completed last year, a magnificent sight. Currently, Chinese and foreign doctors are conducting research in physiology, pathology, and epidemiology, which have already begun. However, due to China's closed society, the availability of materials for pathological anatomy is insufficient, which is a great waste of this research institution.

(2) Shanghai Institute of Natural Sciences: This is one of the cultural projects designated under the Japanese return of the Boxer Indemnity. Naturally, Japanese scientists will jointly lead and conduct research here. The departments related to medicine are pathology, chemistry, and pharmacology. Some shortsighted people in society believe that engaging with the Japanese in this era is ultimately inappropriate. However, we must understand that academia knows no borders and should not be dictated by emotions. Given the perceived lack of purely national research institutes, these kinds of research facilities should be fully utilized and given careful attention.

(3) Forensic Institute of the Ministry of Justice: Located in Zhenru, it is a forensic research institution run by the ministry. It also accepts commissioned examination cases from various courts. I hope society recognizes the true principles of modern forensics so that bizarre articles promoting the "Washing Away of Wrongs" will not reappear as they did a few years ago with a certain lawyer.

(4) Department of Materia Medica Research, Peking Research Institute: The Peking Research Institute is organized similarly to the Academia Sinica. Due to the current situation, part of it has moved to Shanghai. Currently, the Department of Materia Medica is temporarily housed within the Sino-French University's School of Pharmacy. However, legitimate research on Chinese medicine is a slow process, unlike cunning merchants who casually call their products "scientific Chinese medicine," slapping a scientific label on anything and considering the matter settled. The public should pay attention to and urge on this type of research institution, rather than disliking their slowness and instead believing in quick fixes from false science.

(5) Hygiene Testing Laboratory: Both this and the Health Testing Laboratory of the British and French Concession Municipal Council are municipal health organizations. Given that they have research facilities and ample materials, if experts dedicate themselves to hard work there, they can certainly make significant contributions to academia.

In addition, some private research laboratories established by Chinese and foreigners are mostly half business (performing various testing work for practicing doctors) and half research. While it's not to say they have no advanced research to conduct, they face various economic and personnel difficulties, leading them to be short-lived. It's estimated that only seven or eight such laboratories currently exist in Shanghai.

The Western Application of Traditional Chinese Medicine (Continued) 195

— Zhou Mengbai

(X) (1) Bitter Orange Peel (Aurantii Amari Cortex)

Origin: This product is the pericarp of the Rutaceae plant Citrus Aurantium Lunn'e, peeled and dried when unripe.

Properties: This product consists of thin, sharp, oval or strip-shaped slices, with a yellowish-brown, reddish-brown, or greenish-brown exterior. It exhibits numerous small pits and a dense network of ridges. The interior is pale white, with fine lines formed by numerous vascular bundles. It has a pleasant odor and a fragrant, bitter taste.

Composition: This product contains approximately 1.25% bitter orange peel oil, the main component of which is limonene (C10H16). Hesperidin (C22H26O12) (a glycoside) is widely distributed in the pericarp of Rutaceae plants and is also present in bitter orange peel.

Test: If a powder of this product is treated with sodium hydroxide solution, it will immediately turn yellow.

Effects: This product is an aromatic stomachic, used to flavor and deodorize. (Attached old saying) Sour and cold, non-toxic, it lowers qi, reduces accumulation, and kills hernia and worms.

(X) (2) Sweet Orange Peel (Aurantii Dulcis Cortex)

Origin: This product is the pericarp of the Rutaceae plant Citrus Aurantium var. Simehsis Linn'e, peeled when ripe and with the white part of the interior removed. The older the better, hence the name "aged peel" (Chen Pi).

Properties: This product consists of sharp, oval slices, with a dark yellow or orange-yellow exterior and a whitish interior. It has an extremely strong, rich aroma and a pungent, fragrant taste.

Composition: The composition of this product is similar to that of bitter orange peel, containing fine essences consisting of d-limonene (more than 90%) and the glycoside hesperidin. Effects: This product is an aromatic stomachic. The fresh product can be used as a raw material for the manufacture of orange peel oil (Oleum Aurantii).

(Attached old saying) Pungent disperses, bitter dries, warm tonifies and harmonizes. It tonifies with tonifying herbs, drains with draining herbs, rises with rising herbs, and descends with descending herbs. It is a medicine for the qi aspect of the spleen and lungs, treating hundreds of diseases, all by virtue of its qi-regulating and dampness-drying effects.

Jottings from After Consultations (Continued) 196

— Chen Fangzhi

Regarding the second aspect of their speaking ill of me, I also need not defend myself. One can understand from my Q&A with the patient that I did not definitely advise her to go to Shanghai. Even if the trip to Shanghai went terribly wrong, it was she who walked into the trap herself. As for saying my medical skills are not good, I will describe the details of the uterine examination that day. Her cervical os was not a small, round, or oval shape. It was an irregularly curved, elongated shape, with obvious infiltrative thickening and swelling on the sides. The slightly everted mucosal surface was bleeding. When pressed with a finger, it felt relatively soft and fragile, which is a sign of an aggressive type of cancer. Given these observations, any gynecologist would be responsible for noting it. For women over forty with a history of irregular uterine bleeding, any doctor would know to be mindful of tumors. The question of whether one's medical skills are advanced is simply irrelevant.

If they had gone to Shanghai and consulted a reputable and reliable gynecologist who said it wasn't cancer, or if after her death they had an autopsy performed that said it wasn't uterine cancer, then I would willingly accept their scolding. Unfortunately, they did not do that. They do not blame the delay of a certain large hospital, but instead speak ill of me, who had completely fulfilled my duties. Their psychology is truly difficult to understand. Perhaps they feared that the certain large hospital was foreign-run.

Chinese people still view doctors with a perception akin to that of the "three religions and nine streams" (a derogatory term for people of various occupations). Especially doctors in local public hospitals are seen as both traveling healers and public servants. Local gentry call upon them at will, dismiss them at will, criticize them at will, without even asking about the facts. And doctors, upon entering the doors of the gentry, often find that their results are even worse. There must be various causes and effects in this. I recall Guo Yu of the Han Dynasty, who treated the poor and lowly with all his heart and strength, but sometimes could not cure the nobles. He said, "The noble is in a high position and looks down upon his subjects. The subject is fearful and apprehensive. There are four difficulties in treating him, the first being self-serving and not trusting others." Bian Que also had six types of patients he would not treat, one of which was those who were arrogant and did not listen to reason. Two thousand years later, China is still the same. There are many such examples in the world today. No matter how sincerely and truthfully you treat him and tell him the truth, if he is in a bad mood, he will take it out on you. For example, if someone has venereal disease, you examine his urine, test his blood, fulfill your duties completely, and obtain ample evidence to tell him he has gonorrhea or syphilis, he will leave in a rage. People in the world like to be deceived and kept in the dark.

Several Important Discoveries and Inventions in the Development of Modern Medicine and Pharmacy (VIII) 197

— Gu Shoubai

(V) Organ Therapy and Secretion Theory

In European countries, especially Switzerland and Norway, many residents have very large swellings on the front of their throats; this is goiter. Previously, it was unknown what the thyroid gland did, but in 1883, Reverdin noticed that this gland was closely related to the body. Some patients who had their enlarged thyroid glands removed developed many strange symptoms. Initially, they felt tired, which gradually worsened. Even the slightest effort made them feel exhausted, and all work had to be stopped. At this point, they became completely inactive. At the same time, the feeling of cold gradually increased, and later, the body temperature even dropped below normal. Meanwhile, the subcutaneous tissue gradually expanded with a gelatinous liquid, causing the shape to become swollen and the facial features to change greatly. Due to reduced sweat, the skin became very dry, and mental function also decreased, with dulled comprehension. This disease with these symptoms is called myxedema. Examining the thyroid gland of these patients, it is highly atrophied; therefore, when the thyroid gland is removed or naturally atrophies, these symptoms can be triggered. At this time, injecting an extract of sheep thyroid gland under the skin of these patients can reduce or eliminate these symptoms.

From the above facts and many other observations, it can be known that this thyroid gland can secrete a substance that is transported throughout the body by blood vessels, playing a very important role in both physical and mental aspects. This is evidence of the thyroid gland's obvious endocrine function.

In many places in Europe, regardless of whether there are goiter-affected areas, the physical development of children is often extremely poor; this is called cretinism. There are two different conditions for the occurrence of cretinism: one is accompanied by goiter, and the other is without goiter; the latter is specifically called sporadic cretinism. This condition can also occur in areas without goiter.

Patients with cretinism may reach the age of twenty or so, but their height is only equivalent to that of children in the same family who are twelve or sixteen years younger than them, and the decline in mental development is also the same. They cannot read, and they do not even recognize the alphabet. Their speech is also undeveloped, and their shape is swollen and clumsy. In fact, these patients are representatives of small-scale myxedema. These children with cretinism have no thyroid gland; therefore, we can say that this form of cretinism is caused by congenital lack of the thyroid gland.

If this explanation is correct, then using an extract of the thyroid gland should improve the condition of these sick children. If the patient has not been sick for a long time, approximately after treatment with an appropriate amount of thyroid extract, they can grow rapidly, and mental function can generally develop similarly. The earlier these thyroid agents are used for patients, the more obvious these beneficial effects will be.

When initially considering using thyroid extract to treat myxedema, it was thought that it had to be injected under the skin to be effective. Later, it was learned that simply administering the thyroid extract or the thyroid gland itself orally could also achieve the same effect. In the early stages of human evolution, the thyroid gland once had a duct that could inject secretions into the laryngeal cavity, and people in the past had long known that swallowing the thyroid gland through the mouth had an effect that was very similar to that of subcutaneous injection. Today, this thyroid gland is often taken orally and has long been proven to be of great value for myxedema.

Thyroid extract can also be used for other diseases. For example, it seems to have some effect on certain skin diseases, and for other conditions, it has also been proven that this thyroid extract is useful.

Another example of endocrine function is the so-called adrenal gland. These are small bodies located on the upper end of the left and right kidneys and are not connected. If these organs have pathological changes, especially when the condition is progressing deeply, a strange phenomenon will occur in the body. Patients feel very weak and often have vomiting and anemia. Another more obvious phenomenon is that the surface of the skin shows a dirty bronze color; this disease is called Addison's Disease. These unpleasant symptoms are definitely related to the atrophy of the adrenal gland. It is now known that the function of this adrenal gland is caused by endocrine function. Initially, it was thought to be related to the nervous system, which was naturally wrong.

There is no doubt that this adrenal extract has a powerful effect on the body. This substance, called adrenaline, can strongly constrict all small blood vessels, so it is very useful for preventing bleeding from small blood vessels. Scholars have also proven that this extract can constrict peripheral blood vessels to increase blood pressure, so it is quite effective in treating low blood pressure. If the dose of adrenal extract is too large or used for too long, it can cause serious symptoms; this is also something that doctors should pay attention to.

Diabetes, which was always considered to be of unknown cause, was also proven a few years ago by Professor Banting of the University of Toronto in the United States to be caused by endocrine disorders of the islets of Langerhans in the pancreas. He created a type of insulin to treat severe cases of this disease, which was very effective; this is also a great invention in organ therapy.

(VI) X-rays

In December 1895, a very startling piece of news was suddenly published in German newspapers, saying that Professor Röntgen of the University of Würzburg had discovered a type of light that could penetrate objects; this is what is today called X-rays. Now, I will introduce the process of discovery.

Professor Röntgen has always been very interested in the cathode rays in vacuum tubes studied by Hertz and Lenard. On November 8, 1895, he covered a Crookes vacuum tube with thick black paper and passed an electric current through it. Suddenly, he unintentionally saw a strange dark shadow appear on a piece of paper coated with platinum barium cyanide placed on a chair next to it. The shadow looked like the product of light; however, the vacuum tube was tightly wrapped in thick black paper, so where did the light come from? As a result of his continued research, he determined that it definitely came from the vacuum tube and also knew that it could still emit light even at a distance of two meters. He initially thought that this was a novel light that had not been known by previous people, but since there was no umbra, and it could not be reflected or refracted, it was just a new type of radiation. Later, he carefully studied the nature of this radiation and learned that it had a powerful penetrating force, not only able to penetrate paper, cloth, wood chips, etc., but even human palms and thin metal boxes could be penetrated. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Bed and Coffin 198

— Yan

Both beds and coffins are tools for sleep, but one provides short sleep, and the other provides long sleep. People in the world tend to value coffins and despise beds. The rope beds and bamboo mats of the poor are extremely simple, but once they leave the world forever, the coffin for their long sleep, even if extremely crude, is ultimately worth more than the rope bed or bamboo mat. "The cost of a bed for the rich, even if it reaches tens or hundreds of gold coins, is only for one final farewell. The cost of a coffin is often thousands of gold coins. If steel coffins or glass coffins are used, the cost will be even greater. Not only do ordinary people value coffins and despise beds, but even our Confucius had such thoughts. We can know this from his selling his own carriage to make a coffin for Yan Hui.

I speculate that people despise beds and value coffins because they believe there are all kinds of pleasures in life. At home and away, there are pleasant things everywhere. Only after death will they sleep forever, cut off from all pleasures. They can only give him a good coffin so that he can sleep comfortably and contentedly. In fact, this thought is greatly mistaken. In today's world, it is best to grasp reality in everything. There is no need to chase after the past, and there is no need to speculate about the future.

One should grasp the happiness of reality and not speculate about future happiness. The bed is a real thing, so it should be studied carefully. If you don't have money on hand, selling a good bed should also take seven or eight tenths of the future coffin costs to contribute to it, so that the short sleeping bed is better than the long sleeping coffin.

Some say: Short sleep is temporary death, and long sleep is permanent death. Both are death, and both are death without knowing, so why be generous with the bed and stingy with the coffin? I say: You know one thing but not the other. If you fall into sleep, you will naturally be like the dead and unaware. When getting on the bed, one may not necessarily fall asleep immediately, and there are also those who do not want to fall asleep. A nap at noon is taken to rest. Meeting an old friend, after cutting candles by the west window, continuing with long talks foot to foot. If it is a refined bed, what will the happiness be like? On the bed, there is also the greatest work in the problems of life. If it is not a suitable bed, what is the flaw in perfection? In addition, those who govern people in bed can govern the country and pacify the world in bed. They can also sign armistice agreements in bed, and people even express political views in bed. In short, the function of the bed is not just for temporary death and sleep. As for permanent death, unless your body is like our national father and has the qualifications to not decay, it is worthy of being placed in a good coffin. Otherwise, the remains will decay and disappear in two or three days. Is it worth placing them in a good coffin? Therefore, I advise people to do their best to study their beds before they die. The coffin after death must be frugally entrusted to the children and grandchildren when they are about to die.

Under the Lamp 199

— Ding'an

Towns and villages are now in the most financially depleted state. Not to mention extravagant consumption, which was abolished long ago. Even the electric lights used for illumination at night have mostly had their lines cut by the company, and they have been changed to kerosene lamps. Some better ones use gasoline lamps, but these are a minority. When the shopkeeper is gloomily under the kerosene lamp at night, tapping the abacus and carefully checking the day's business, the result is a long sigh, because even the capital is not enough to cover expenses.

Farmers, even now in such a civilized society, still adhere to ancient customs. It can be said that some families have absolutely no concept of time. They "work at sunrise and rest at sunset." Therefore, they rarely light lamps at night. Even if they need to use them, they mostly use vegetable oil lamps or red candles. Sometimes when performing martial arts shows or shadow plays in the village, the shadow play, which is made by paper-cut figures threaded on strings and projected onto a sheepskin frame, is lit with smoky kerosene lanterns or red candles.

Our friends in Shanghai can be said to be extremely pleasure-seeking. The bright electric lights, with light bulbs of different sizes, different colors, frosted and milky white, tubular and round, have various types. There are even many differences in the lampshades outside. The waste of a single lamp is so great that comparing it to the people in the interior is probably like the difference between heaven and hell!

People seeking a living in Shanghai are also sighing bitterly. Every day, within the office hours of X a.m. to X p.m., they are accompanied by the long days and electric lights. Thinking of opening electric lights in the house during the daytime has almost become a very common fact. Speaking of it, one can only feel sadness. The eyes of the average young person are under those electric lights every day. In the near future, their eyesight will definitely weaken, and at the very least, they will suffer from eye diseases.

Of course, there are also many people who seek pleasure under the lights. Look at the dancers in the dance halls, the gamblers in the casinos, the drinkers in the hotels, the travelers in the inns. They are intoxicated in the vortex of the enchanting lights, unaware of their own needs and how critical the country is, and are wholeheartedly enjoying themselves. I think they should reflect on themselves if they have any sober moments!

Under the bleak and dim alley streetlights, there are singing girls who have lost their youth. Under the store lights of the street stores, there are strong men whose glory has passed. These people, not long ago, were wildly frivolous under the bright electric lights. How long ago was it that the lights are still the same, but people have changed! Oh, lights, lights! Is this your sin, or is it the general population's "self-inflicted sin, unable to live?"

A Tipsy Night 200

— Anfu

Was it the kindness of friends? They made me almost drunk! In a new autumn evening sky.

With blurred, drunken eyes and staggering steps, I dragged my shadow along the silent sidewalk, swaying; the light breeze slipping down from the treetops kissed my face, kissed my hair, so tender! Like the tenderness of a spring breeze. How fast! Light steps had already carried me to my dwelling.

Who is in my room, the light so bright? When I walked into the bedroom, I realized it was not the lamplight, but the moonlight shining through the glass window. While taking off my coat and changing into my pajamas, I thought, how could I be so muddled tonight, drinking myself so drunk, I should go to bed early! So I climbed into bed. But as soon as I lay down, I felt my nerves twitching especially fast; it felt like something was crawling in my heart, and my mouth seemed to be frying; unable to sleep soundly, I had to get up again. After drinking tea, I pushed open the window, and the flowers, plants, and trees in the neighbor's backyard came into view. Although I was used to seeing them every day, they didn't evoke any special feelings; but in the moonlight, they seemed much quieter and more secluded than in the sunlight, and the most charming were the roses, lowering their heads as if smiling at me. I remembered the garden in my hometown, with flowers, plants, and trees, and in the clear, moonlit nights, I also wandered and pondered. Now, my hometown is far away from me, and in the hazy moonlight, I couldn't help but feel a lingering homesickness.

The wind, a gust colder than the last, flew over my body, and a slight chill permeated my heart. The cry of "Don't catch a cold" was not to be heard, and the person to put a coat on me was not there; besides myself, who else would take care of me? For my own sake, I should add a coat; so I casually took a thicker shirt from the rack and put it on, still leaning against the window, watching the moon in the sky, and listening to the sounds of the insects on the ground.

It must be almost two o'clock, right? The whole city was in silence; in the depths of the branches, there was a corner of a small building, and the light in the building suddenly turned on. On the thin window screen, there was a graceful figure taking off her evening gown, piece by piece; whose daughter was it?

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 201

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: Guests Depart, Shyness Lingers, Tender Feelings Evoked by a Smile

Visitors Arrive, Old Grievances Stir, Bad News Brings Sorrow

Unexpectedly, one minute, two minutes passed, fifteen minutes passed, and still these two had not returned. Guizhi sat there doing nothing, and Zhao Ziqiang had even less courage to speak. So he coughed a couple of times and sniffled a few times. However, such attempts at conversation took up very little time, and after the sounds passed, he perhaps felt especially bored. Guizhi looked at his appearance, wanting to laugh but unable to. So she took out her handkerchief from her pocket and gently wiped her mouth. Then she raised her hand and patted her hair, turning her face towards the door and saying, "Where did they go? Why is there no news at all?" Zhao Ziqiang took this opportunity and chimed in, "They all like to joke around, maybe they just left." Guizhi lowered her head, raised her eyelids to look at Zhao Ziqiang, and did not say anything. Zhao Ziqiang reached into his pockets and rummaged around, taking out a pack of cigarettes, and then looked around for matches. He struck a match and slowly lit one. He had just exhaled a puff of smoke, and had a sentence he wanted to say, when Guizhi, supporting herself on the edge of the table, suddenly stood up and said to Zhao Ziqiang in a serious tone, "I want to go back." The tone in which she said these words was very firm. However, the voice she uttered was very soft, so soft that almost even she herself could not hear it. But Zhao Ziqiang was very clever this time and actually heard it. He nodded to Guizhi and said, "Sit for a while longer. Maybe they will come back." Guizhi said, "They are deliberately joking around. They have been gone for so long with no news. They won't come back." Zhao Ziqiang had no choice but to stand up and said, "If there is nothing important to do back at your residence, then why not sit for a while longer?" His eyes were watching Guizhi very attentively, but his face was slightly turned away, not looking directly at Guizhi. Guizhi smiled slightly, bit her lip, and sat down again. (183)

Words of a Fool

Smoking cigarettes can earn rewards of ten thousand or five thousand, so children with runny noses are all smoking cigarettes. I think that in the future, coffin shops and medicine shops will also have prize tickets attached, along with various benefits.

Now, cigarette cases are more valuable than cigarettes because a few cigarette cases offer the hope of hundreds or thousands of yuan, naturally making them as valuable as bank checks.

This is also an enthusiastic supporter of nudity in the education world. Free Talk

Lessons from the Movies 203

— Runiu

When I watched old Chinese operas in my hometown village, I had not yet been educated to be a "scholar," and the children were mostly farmers. What we loved to watch were somersaults, tiger leaps, and a puff of smoke revealing a demon; the plot didn't seem to have much to do with us. The fight for cities and lands between the Da Mian (painted face) and Laosheng (old male role), and the separations and reunions of the Xiaosheng (young male role) and Zhengdan (main female role), were all their affairs. Children who grasped hoe handles knew that they would never ascend the platform to be generals or go to the capital to take exams. But I still remember a play that moved me, it seemed to be called "Chopping Wood to Show Sincerity." A high official was wrongly accused and was about to be killed, and an old family servant in his family, who looked very similar, went to "face the law" in his place. The tragic actions and songs really touched the hearts of the viewers, making them discover a good model for themselves. Because the farmers in my hometown, once the busy farming season was over, some would go to help the wealthy. In order to act the part, before the execution, the mistress of the house had to "hold the head and cry loudly" as usual, but he kicked her away. Even at this time, the proper roles had to be strictly observed. This was a loyal servant, a righteous person, a good person.

But when I watched movies in Shanghai, I had already become a "lower-class Chinese." Looking at the white people and rich people sitting upstairs, and the middle and lower-class "Chinese stomachs" lined up downstairs, the screen showed white soldiers fighting, white masters getting rich, white ladies getting married, white heroes exploring, making the viewers admire, envy, be terrified, and feel that they could not do it themselves. But when white heroes explored Africa, there was often a black loyal servant who paved the way for him, served him, risked his life, and died for him, allowing the master to return home safely. When he prepared for a second expedition, a loyal servant could no longer be found, so he remembered the deceased, his face darkened, and a black face from his memory appeared on the screen. The viewers also mostly darkened their faces in the dim light: they were moved.

Fortunately, domestic films are also struggling to rise, jumping up and over high walls, raising their hands and throwing out flying swords, but this also withdrew from Shanghai along with the 19th Route Army. Now they are preparing to screen Turgenev's "Spring Torrents" and Mao Dun's "Spring Silkworms." Of course, this is progress. But at this time, there came a heavily promoted "Yao Mountain Love History."

The theme of this film is "civilizing the Yao people," and the key is "recruiting a son-in-law," which reminds people of "Si Lang Visits His Mother" and "Princess Shuangyang Pursues Di." The great theory that Chinese spiritual civilization dominates the world is not often heard these days. If you want to civilize, you can only retreat to the Miao and Yao people, and to achieve this great cause, you must first "marry." The descendants of the Yellow Emperor, like black people, cannot marry the princesses of European and Asian powers, so spiritual civilization cannot be spread. This is something that everyone can understand from this.

Simplification and Internationalization of English — Qian Gechuan 204

Mr. Suoyuan has published two articles in a row, and I only took the time to respond once. I have answered the two points he raised in the first article one by one. The second article deliberately quibbled and nitpicked, and I also explained it to him. But today (the 7th), I saw that Mr. Suoyuan had come again, saying that I had "not answered" but was "fooling around" with him. In fact, just in the Free Talk publication alone, you gentlemen have come four times in a row, and I have only answered once. If we're talking about "fooling around," I really don't dare to accompany you. As for saying that there is a real argument that wants me to answer, I am willing to join the discussion. So this time, after reading the articles by both Mr. Shi Zhi and Mr. Suoyuan, although I understood a little of the meaning of the two words "fooling around," and felt that the attitude lacked gentlemanly demeanor, I did not use the shield of the son to attack the spear of the son, and take these two words as the topic. The title above is enough to show that I am entirely out of academic discussion, and does not contain the slightest malice.

Mr. Suoyuan said that I acknowledged two points, namely (1) Basic English is not an international language, and (2) the two have their own strengths and weaknesses, and their own grounds. But I did not acknowledge the first point. Ogden created this language entirely for international use, but what we now find most useful in it is its simplicity. As for whether it can achieve the effect of international use, that is even better of two things at once. Why can Basic English be used as an international language? Because in European and American countries, English is commonly spoken, and even in Japan it is possible. A friend of mine travelled in Japan in the first year of the Great Earthquake and used English throughout. What about China? Shanghai is an exception for the moment. Even in the inland, if you are sick and go to the hospital, and you want water when it is hot, no matter how many times you shout "Akvo," it is unlikely that someone will bring you water. In the end, if the nurse gets impatient and comes to interfere, if you say she shouldn't look angry ("Kolera"), she might mistake you for having cholera and give you a few injections of saline. As long as you learn the word "Water" in Basic English, you won't suffer this kind of hardship. It is commonly used in both the East and the West, isn't that an international language?

I learned Esperanto twelve years ago. I know very well the difference between it and Basic English, so I said that each has its strengths and weaknesses, and each has its own grounds. The content of Basic English has been discussed in many books and in Mr. Zhang's articles, so I will not mention it here due to space limitations. Let me talk about the strengths and weaknesses of "Esperanto" and its grounds. Its strength is that its grammar is extremely simple, and the changes are regular. Its weakness is that it is still too early and not widely used. Even the mixing of written and spoken language is too little writing for us to read. As for its grounds, I am afraid that at present it can only be used, as Mr. Suoyuan said, to shout slogans at the International Workers' Games held in Moscow. Because Russian is too difficult, it cannot force people to learn it well, so it uses "Esperanto" to communicate with the proletariat of various countries in the world. So "Moscow Impressions" and "Travels in New Russia" are also made by it.

Mr. Suoyuan said that he agreed with the above two points. Let's talk about the five points that he did not agree with. (1) I have answered the following regarding Basic English's attempt to be an international language. As for Basic English's attempt to be a rationalized scheme for English, which is also his following three or four items, I will now reply in detail separately: Regarding the rationalization of spelling, I have said that even Anglo failed, so Ogden changed his course and started from other aspects. It is well known that getting familiar with something is good, so Basic English does not create new words. Instead of finding a new group of people to learn the word "Rit," it is better to retain the existing five hundred million people who already know the word "Right." This is precisely the rational approach. Habit becomes nature, and nature is the most rational. Foreigners eat bread, Chinese people eat rice, can you say who is irrational? So the spelling "Right" is rational because it evolved from 1610 through various changes of "Riht." If it is changed to "Rit," it becomes unreasonable. As for the exceptions of irregular verbs and the minority of nouns, although they cannot completely conform to the principles of artificial language, they have their own reasons. Some are due to pronunciation. In short, we only need to check the traces of the development of OE, ME, and MlnE to understand. (2) Mr. Suoyuan said that Basic English cannot be separated from ordinary English and cannot replace ordinary English. I cannot agree with this either, because if you learn Basic English, you can speak, write letters, write articles, and use it for various purposes. Why can't it be independent? Even regarding the latter, since we can use Basic English to translate ordinary English books and use it to speak ordinary English, why can't it replace it? Finally, (5) no matter what the environment is, it is in the heart, not in the language, that one wants to subordinate people. Although Japan forced Koreans to learn Japanese, the Koreans were not convinced because of it. Conversely, the Russians can also win over many obedient people by using "Esperanto" instead of their national language.

Autumn Dreams on a Literary Bed 205

— Youguang

Spring dreams are topsy-turvy. What about "A Midsummer Night's Dream"? Looking at Shakespeare's plays, it is still topsy-turvy. Chinese autumn dreams, as a rule, should be "bleak and chilling." Before the Republic, death row inmates were all "executed after autumn," which was following the seasons. Heaven teaches people to do this, and people cannot but do this. So-called "literati" are of course no exception. Eating their fill and sleeping in bed, the food cannot be completely digested, so they dream, and since it is autumn now, heaven teaches their dreams to be solemn.

In the thirty-first issue of Volume 2 of "Wave Sounds" (published on August 12), there is a letter to the editor from a Mr. "Lin Ding," which says in part:

"...the dispute, who is right and who is wrong, outsiders cannot know the details. However, mutual destruction, as seen by onlookers, cannot but be acknowledged as the misfortune of the entire literary scene... I believe that everyone should first be spanked a hundred times to serve as a warning, and all other matters can be left unmentioned..."

The other day, there was also an unsigned editorial in a certain tabloid, which was also very angry about the Yu-Zhao plagiarism dispute some time ago:

"...if I were to seize power one day, I would definitely arrest these people and sentence them to hard labor, reading books for ten years; the Chinese literary scene might still have a day of cleanliness."

Zhang Xianzhong was about to decline himself, so his actions did not ask "who is right and who is wrong," he simply killed. Qing Dynasty officials, regardless of whether the two parties were right or wrong, did occasionally beat each party a hundred or fifty times, because the Manchus still wanted slaves to provide plunder. This is Mr. "Lin Ding's" old dream. The nameless Mr. in a certain tabloid is even more civilized, at least, he already knows the Shanghai Municipal Council's method of "fining" lower-class Chinese.

But the first question is how can one "seize power one day"? How can weak scholars manage to become powerful ministers? Previously, one could hope to recruit a son-in-law and suddenly rise to prominence, but now there are no emperors, and even if one covers their face with snow cream, they will never encounter the favor of a princess; at most, they can only hope to become the son-in-law of a wealthy family, and the method of buying an official rank has long been abolished. For "great power," one can only look up at the grapes on high like a fox. The integrity and cleanliness of the literary scene is probably very remote.

During the May Fourth Movement, "literary beggars" were discovered in the publishing industry, followed by "literary vagrants." But this kind of imposing figure is what I have newly discovered in Shanghai this autumn. Unable to name them, I will tentatively call them "literary officials." Looking at literary history, the literary scene often has times of integrity and cleanliness, but who has ever seen this purification of the literary scene have the slightest relationship with these kinds of "literary officials"?

However, dreams can always be made, fortunately they don't matter much, and writing them out is interesting. Rest in peace, prospective young masters!

Quarrel 206

— Zhao Zhengdong

The woman was preparing dinner in the kitchen.

The man came back from outside, leaned against the door frame, and spaced out, with a look of frustration on his face.

"Were the rice plants in the field weighed? How much was it in the end?" the woman asked resentfully.

"Twenty dan, almost," the man's voice was very low, almost inaudible.

"Twenty dan, almost?" the woman stopped her work, staring at the man's face. "Good, twenty mu of land, not even twenty dan! See how you plan to get through this year?"

"..." The man's eyes were closed. But crystal beads had already appeared in his eye sockets.

"I told you not to plant rice, to plant cotton. You didn't listen, saying something about how planting cotton was very risky, and if there was a western flood in the autumn, you wouldn't get anything. Has there been a western flood now?" the woman said, getting angrier and angrier. "You also said something about the chief, something about officials, something about buying a lot of foreign cotton and coming back, saying something about how the price of cotton this year was sure to be cut. You wanted to plant rice. Now planting rice is good, not even eight dou per mu, but paying the rent takes one dan; and there are still debts to be paid, and busy work has to be paid for! See what you're going to do?"

"How did I know that the rice would have so many weeds? I'm not a god," he was a little embarrassed and angry, his eyes widening, and several crystal beads rolled down one after another. "Who wants you to be a god! If you had listened to me and planted cotton, it wouldn't be like this."

"What else are you going to say? It's already the plaque in the City God Temple, 'It's too late to regret.' We'll plant cotton next year."

"Next year! But how are we going to get through this year?"

"If we can't get through it, we'll die!"

Shallow Lake (1) 207

— Written by Joseph Conrad of England, translated by Shi Heng

The white man rested his arms on the top of the small cabin at the stern of the boat, and said to the helmsman:

"Let's spend the night at the Asata settlement. It's getting late." The Malay only responded with a sound, and continued to stare at the water. The white man put his chin on his crossed arms, watching the waves stirred up by the hull of the boat. At the end of the straight row of trees, which were cut off by the shimmering of the river, the sun, as if not covered by clouds, dazzled the eyes, and rested low on the water, the surface of the water was as smooth as a metal band. The forest, gloomy and dark, stood quietly on both sides of the wide river. Next to the towering giant tree roots, a kind of palm tree without a trunk, supporting heavy clusters of large leaves, grew out of the mud on the shore, motionless and suspended over the swirling water. In the still air, every tree, every leaf, every branch, and every small petal, seemed to be frozen in a state of complete stillness as if by magic. On the water, apart from the eight oars that regularly flashed and rocked up, and then splashed into the water together, there was nothing else moving; at the same time, the helmsman quickly and regularly used force to swing his paddle left and right, drawing a shining semicircle over his head. The stirred-up river water made a chaotic gurgling sound, washing up foam along the river bank. Thus, the white man's canoe proceeded between the momentary whirlpools stirred up by itself, as if entering the port of a land that was forever separated from the memory of turbulence.

The white man, turned his back to the setting sun, watching the empty and vast water surface. About in this last three-mile journey, the turbulent river, as if powerless to resist, was seduced by the free and vast horizontal line, and flowed straight into the sea, straight to the east 丨丨 to the east that contains light and shadow. At the stern, towards a small bird's frequent cry 丨丨 a disharmonious and weak chirping, before he reached the other side, it brushed across the flat water surface and disappeared into the silence of the surrounding nature.

The helmsman, held the paddle tightly with his stiff arm, paddling in the water, his body bent forward. The water made a gurgling sound; suddenly the straight river line seemed to spin from the center, the forest swayed in a semicircle, and then the slanting light of the setting sun, emitting a fiery red glow, shone on the side of the canoe, and projected the slender and crooked shadows of the sailors on the shimmering river. The white man looked up ahead. The progress of the boat changed direction, forming a right angle with the river, and the carved dragon head of the bow turned to the gap in the bushes surrounding the river bank. The boat glided, skimming over the thin branches hanging in the air, disappearing from the river as if a slender amphibious animal was about to leave the water and seek a den in the forest.
