Economics Special Publication Published Every Sunday Issue 39

Foreign Trade This Year and Speculations on the Future 208

— Hou Pei

The Customs Statistical Abstract has already published monthly figures for foreign trade in the first half of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). In these past six months, looking at the present and reflecting on the past, we cannot help but feel pessimistic. Although the economic depression of the world is a common phenomenon in various countries, and China cannot escape this exception, our country's trade is, proportionally, trending downwards. In the past two years, the low silver price has indeed been a great opportunity to promote export trade. At the same time, the Chinese people have spared no effort in promoting domestic goods, which should have resulted in considerable progress. However, with the decline of industry and commerce and the withering of all trades, export trade is becoming more and more sluggish. This situation is a full manifestation of the decline of our national economy, and we should not shy away from admitting it.

The total trade volume for the first half of this year: exports were valued at more than 296.46 million yuan, and imports were valued at more than 396.07 million gold units, equivalent to more than 771.10 million national currency yuan, totaling more than 1,067.57 million yuan. In the first half of last year (1932), foreign trade: exports were 29.89 million taels of Customs silver, equivalent to 465.72 million national currency yuan, and imports were 52.905 million gold units, equivalent to 945.879 million yuan, totaling more than 1,411.599 million yuan. Comparing the two years, trade this year, both exports and imports, have decreased. Exports decreased by 169.254015 million yuan, imports decreased by 174.770915 million yuan, and the total decreased by 344.024930 million yuan. In other words, exports decreased by 36.34 percent, imports decreased by 18.48 percent, and the total decreased by 24.38 percent. According to the trade statistics report of the International Trade Bureau, comparing the first six months of this year with the same months of last year, during the six months, the highest export volume was only equal to 83.33 percent of the same month last year (January), and the lowest was only equal to 48.00 percent of the same month last year (April). The highest import volume exceeded the same month last year by 18.66 percent (only in February), and the lowest was only equal to 62.99 percent of the same month last year (January). The total highest only exceeded the same month last year by 2 percent, and the lowest was only equal to 66.34 percent of last year. The degree of difference from last year is obvious. Some say that this year's trade statistics cannot be compared equally with last year because the reports from the Northeast Customs are incomplete. If the Northeast Customs are included, the trade figures may even be higher than this year. Let us try to compare again by including the Northeast Customs. According to the investigation, in the first six months of last year, the figures for the Northeast Customs were: exports valued at 198,450,504 yuan, imports valued at 113,605,993 yuan, totaling 312,056,497 yuan. If we assume that the reported figures of the Northeast Customs in this year's trade are still comparable to last year, and include them in the calculation of last year's figures, then the trade in the first six months of this year should be: exports 494,917,023 yuan, imports 884,714,078 yuan, totaling 1,379,631,101 yuan. Comparing this number with the first half of the year, exports increased by 29.196 million yuan, imports decreased by 61.1649 million yuan, and the total decreased by 31.968 million yuan, which is still 2.27 percent lower than last year. It is even more obvious that this year's trade is not as good as last year. Moreover, the increase in trade in the southern customs since last year has a considerable impact on the seizure of the Northeast Customs. Although the extent of the impact cannot be determined, it does not seem too low to add the figures of the Northeast Customs. This is another point that we should pay attention to.

Among the figures calculated by including the Northeast Customs, export trade should have increased by 29 million yuan compared to last year, and the situation is more advanced than last year. However, according to the actual figures for this year, exports decreased by 36 percent, which is more than imports. The reason is that the quantity of exports in the Northeast Customs is large, and soybeans alone account for a large proportion of our country's exports. The seizure of the Northeast Customs means that the soybean trade is equal to zero. Previously accounting for more than 15 percent of the total export value, it now accounts for only 0.73 percent. This has a major impact on this year's export trade. This is why the figures including the Northeast Customs exceed last year. Now, let's try to compare the figures excluding the Northeast Customs. In the first six months of last year, excluding the Northeast Customs, exports should have been 267.27 million yuan, imports should have been 832.273 million yuan, and the total should have been 1,099.543 million yuan. Comparing the upper period of this year with the same period last year, exports should increase by 10.92 percent, imports should decrease by 7.35 percent, and the total should decrease by 2.97 percent. This point also shows that, judging from the proportion, the progress of export trade is indeed better than import trade, which is quite satisfactory.

The deficit in the first half of this year was 474.641566 million yuan, compared to 30.8189 million taels of Customs silver last year, equivalent to 480.158467 million yuan. The number this year is slightly lower by more than 5.517 million yuan. However, the percentage of deficit is higher than last year. The deficit in the first half of this year accounted for 61.55 percent of the total import value, while last year it accounted for 50.76 percent, which is enough to prove the high proportion of deficit this year. However, we should also pay attention to the fact that the figures of the Northeast Customs are not within the scope of this year's report. If the figures of the Northeast Customs are included, the deficit this year should account for 44.06 percent of the total import value, which is lower than the proportion of deficit last year. If the Northeast Customs are excluded, the deficit in the first half of last year should be 565 million yuan, accounting for 67.89 percent of the import value, and the degree of deficit is obviously higher than this year. From this situation, the seriousness of the deficit problem this year does not seem to exceed that of last year, and the situation is the same as export trade.

It is still difficult to predict the amount of the deficit this year. If we infer from the increase or decrease ratio of each quarter of last year, the third quarter decreased by 32.95 percent compared to the second quarter, and the fourth quarter decreased by 4.48 percent compared to the third quarter. If there is no special change in the second half of this year, and the trade pattern is roughly the same as last year, then the estimated deficit for the whole year this year will be more than 828.7 million yuan, or equal to more than 531.93 million taels of Customs silver, which is slightly lower than the deficit of 556,605,240 taels of Customs silver last year. However, this is under the circumstance that the export figures of the Northeast Customs have fallen miserably. However, what we should pay attention to in the trade in the second half of this year is the 50 million US dollars of cotton and wheat loans. The import of cotton and wheat should increase significantly. Even if not all of it is imported, the amount of the deficit may reach 900 million yuan, which is also unknown.

In our country's foreign trade, Japan has always ranked first. Since last year, the United States has taken the first place, increasing from 18.85 percent (in the 20th year of the Republic) to 21.16 percent (percentage of total trade value), while Japan has decreased from 23.93 percent (in the 20th year of the Republic) to 16.45 percent. In the first half of this year, the United States still ranks first, and Japan ranks second, but the percentages have both decreased. The United States accounts for 19.85 percent (20.94 percent in the same period last year), and Japan accounts for 10.91 percent (18.20 percent in the same period last year). The changes in trade with China by the two countries are huge. Compared with the same period last year, the export ratio of the United States has increased almost doubled, while the import has decreased from 26.51 percent to 20.37 percent. For Japan, the export ratio has decreased from 25.50 percent to 15.11 percent, and the import has decreased from 14.58 percent to 9.31 percent. Other countries, such as Australia, have increased the ratio from 3.04 percent in the same period last year to 7.55 percent, and Russia has decreased from 2.99 percent to 1.63 percent, of which exports have decreased from 7.62 percent to 1.12 percent, and imports have increased from 0.75 percent to 1.83 percent. The decrease in exports should be due to the impact of the Northeast issue. Only the United Kingdom has maintained its original state, with almost no increase or decrease. According to the trade trend this year, the United States' position in the first place is undoubtedly beyond doubt, and with the addition of cotton and wheat loans, the import ratio should increase even more. Even if Japan's trade does not retreat to the third place, the ratio with the United Kingdom will not be far apart. There will not be the high ratio as before. However, this is not Japan's loss, but due to the seizure of the Northeast Customs. Russia has changed from export surplus to import surplus, which has been proved by statistical facts. In the future, even if the export of Chinese goods increases slightly, its ratio will be far less than the speed of import of Russian goods, which can be asserted.

In recent years, our country's foreign trade has had a phenomenon of increasing year by year. In the 20th year of the Republic, it reached the highest number in history, valued at more than 234 million taels of Customs silver. Last year, due to the occurrence of the January 28th Incident and the Rehe Incident, and the incompleteness of the Northeast Customs reports, it fell miserably to more than 154.18 million taels of Customs silver. In the upper period of this year's trade, due to the lack of reports from the Northeast Customs, it has decreased by 34.4 million yuan compared to the same period last year. Even if there is a slight increase in the lower period, the total may be difficult to exceed 220 million yuan, equivalent to more than 141.2 million taels of Customs silver. It is still less than last year, and the decrease should be more than 12.98 million taels of Customs silver, which may be the lowest number in nearly 17 years. In terms of deficit, due to the loss of major exports from the Northeast, it may reach a huge number of 900 million yuan, which is not only the highest number in history, but also exceeds the proportion of last year by a large margin. In the total trade volume of 150 million taels of Customs silver last year, the deficit accounted for 35 percent, while this year it may account for more than 40 percent of the total trade volume. At this critical moment, if the people of the country do not quickly seek remedy, the overseas market may no longer have a foothold for our country's commodities.

Various Countries' Rejection of Japanese Goods and Japan's Defensive War 209

— Zong Fan

I

Since the September 18th Incident in Northeast China, the ferocious face of Japanese imperialism has been revealed to the world. The movement in our country to resist Japanese goods has also become more concrete and widespread. The sales of Japanese goods have suffered an extreme blow, and Japan's export trade has naturally been greatly affected. As a result, difficulties in the operation of various industries have increased, and the number of unemployed has surged. At the same time, panic has spread in the financial and fiscal sectors. The disastrous fall in the international value of Japanese currency and the flight of genuine goods overseas have also become inevitable results. Therefore, in December 1931, Japan decisively banned gold exports again, adopting a policy of currency inflation as a countermeasure to this panic. It used the decline in foreign exchange rates to cause a sharp drop in the prices of Japanese goods in overseas markets and used dumping policies to open up new overseas markets. As a result, it succeeded in stabilizing old markets and expanding new markets in places as near as India, Southeast Asia, and South Africa, and as far as the Mediterranean and South America. In particular, Japan's dumping policies in British colonies have eroded a significant portion of the British goods market.

This inevitably provoked fierce competition between British and Japanese goods. This competition became a movement in Britain to resist Japanese goods, further escalating from an economic struggle to a political one. The first battle in Britain's movement to resist Japanese goods began with India's revision of cotton textile tariffs before the Ottawa Conference in July and August 1932 had concluded. At that time, India's revised cotton textile tariffs were 25% for British products and 50% for all other foreign products. Previously, the difference in tariff rates between British products and products from other countries was only 11.2%, but now it had suddenly increased to 25%. The second battle was the termination of the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty on April 10, 1933. This was followed by the enactment of the Indian Industrial Protection Act on April 12. On June 6, based on this law, the tariffs on cotton textiles from countries other than the seven British nations were raised to 75%, which was the highest tariff rate, effectively prohibiting imports. This was not only the case in India. In Egypt, in May 1933, tariffs on cotton yarn and cotton cloth from countries other than Britain were also increased. On June 15, the Malay Peninsula implemented tariff increases on cotton cloth imports, with a 10% increase on British products, and a 30% increase on high-quality Japanese products, and 70-80% on low-quality products. On June 26, in the British-controlled areas of East Africa, tariffs on cotton textiles and rayon textiles were increased by 20% to 50%. On June 31, the state government of Horwell imposed tariffs on cotton textiles, rubber shoes, condensed milk, canned goods, and other food products from countries other than Britain, while British products were exempt from all taxes. East Africa also imposed the same taxes on Japanese goods as on the highest-priced British cotton textiles. On July 3, New Zealand merchants petitioned for a movement to prevent Japanese goods, and West Africa even abolished previous commercial treaties. From the facts presented above, it can be seen that Britain's rejection and resistance to Japanese goods is spreading like wildfire, expanding and progressing without pause.

From Britain's motivation to build tariff barriers in India, extending to a thorough rejection of Japanese goods throughout its colonies, this is a well-planned and systematic containment and strangulation of Japan's external economy. With such concrete steps in Britain's movement to resist Japanese goods, the economic struggle between Britain and Japan is not only actively mobilizing individual sectors, but in reality, the entire economic front is engaged in a fierce war with short weapons and artillery fire.

II

The so-called economic struggle between Britain and Japan is, in other words, merely a self-defense measure by the mighty British Empire against the activities of Japanese goods. This suggests that Japanese goods must have a strong presence in overseas markets. To answer this question, it is best to quote the contents of the "Survey Report on British-Japanese Industrial Competition" by the Special Investigation Committee of the British Industries Federation:

"(1) Over the next 20 to 30 years, Japan's population is expected to increase by approximately 15 million to 30 million, but its domestic resources can only support a portion of its population. Therefore, the competition of Japanese goods overseas is an inevitable and unquestionable fact.

(2) The tariff barriers of European and American countries are increasing day by day, and Japan is gradually expanding the scope of its exported goods. Therefore, Japan must seize every opportunity to engage in fierce competition with various manufactured goods in the international market.

(3) In order to compete with various countries, Japan does not hesitate to use various means. In the past year, it has consciously used the decline of the Japanese yen to recklessly launch a national sales policy to threaten markets around the world. The first to suffer are the British, but no other trading nation is unaffected.

(4) Differences in wages, labor conditions, and living standards, etc. In terms of the main component of labor costs, commodities, the East and the West cannot compete under the same conditions. To give a relevant example, Japan's rayon industry exports have increased ninefold in the past six years, while Britain's exports have decreased by two-thirds during the same period.

(5) The impact of Japanese attacks on British manufacturers is not limited to rayon and crude cotton textile industries, but also extends to heavy chemical industry products, light bulbs, bicycles, buttons, cement, rubber shoes, etc.

(6) The reasons why Japanese goods are able to drive out British goods: the first and foremost reason is wages, working hours, and labor conditions, etc., because the living standards in the East are extremely low; the second reason is the decline in exchange rates and the implementation of government export subsidies and freight dumping. These are the 'unfair' advantages enjoyed by Japanese exporters.

(7) If there is no joint action or plan to protect the interests of Britain in the British homeland and its colonies; if the competition of Japanese goods is allowed to continue without any attempt to resist it, then the British industrial protection policy and the plan decided by the Ottawa Conference will be equivalent to zero."

Furthermore, the Special Investigation Committee of the Industries Federation, after the aforementioned report, made the following criticisms regarding Japan's labor conditions, and the main points are extracted below:

"(1) Behind the competition of Japanese goods is a large, productive, low-wage labor force. At least their living standards are one-third lower than the labor conditions in Western Europe; and in addition to low wages and labor conditions, Japanese exports are also artificially protected by the state, with special tariffs, subsidies, and state guarantees of profits.

(2) Certain Japanese goods are exempt from income tax for the first four years after the establishment of the factory. The activities of trade commissioners abroad, under the jurisdiction of the Bureau of Commerce, are also most noteworthy.

(3) Japan's subsidies for ocean-going ships, except for those during the years of 1915-1918 and 1920 when the situation was relatively difficult, are enormous subsidies granted by the Japanese government to ocean-going shipping companies, so that they are exempt from various losses, and the number is extremely large.

(4) It is foreseeable that Japan will continue to skillfully use its exchange rate market prices to help the development of its trade.

(5) Japan's cotton textile industry benefits greatly from the surplus of women, while male workers' wages account for only one-third of the British wage rate, and female workers' wage rate is only one-quarter.

(6) Many other Japanese industries still fall within the realm of household industries, such as the porcelain industry, which is noteworthy. According to British manufacturers' reports, Japanese products sold in various markets of the British Empire are priced at less than half the price of British industrial products."

III

The main themes of the economic struggle between Britain and Japan are extremely clear after reading the above report. However, Britain has even more advanced strategies for its struggle against Japan. The following is an excerpt from a speech by Samuel Hanbury in the British House of Commons:

"The competition of Japanese goods is by no means just ordinary commercial competition. It is attacking foreign markets with the creed of economic aggression, concentrating all means to achieve their goals, deliberately enforcing currency inflation, and infringing upon the trademark rights of other countries. Japan wants to dominate the East and even hold the reins of the world market! Our first step is to conclude reciprocal agreements between Britain and its dominions; secondly, to conclude reciprocal tariff agreements with countries such as France, Belgium, and Italy, which are related to the colonial market. We should also seize the opportunity to determine a new direction for British foreign policy; and at the same time, we must have a closer partnership with the United States. I earnestly hope that the government will adopt a consistent approach to deal with the current problems, and make efforts to fight head-on with Japan's fragmentary solutions in a resolute and decisive manner." We can also see from this speech that Britain's movement to resist Japan is becoming more and more acute and concrete. Since the formation of the British economic nationalism group, it has progressed more organizedly, and the economic struggle against Japan has also reached its final stage.

Originally, the formation of the British economic nationalism group, as mentioned above, was the fact decided by the Ottawa Conference in July 1933. Its main points are: to adopt free trade within the British Empire and protectionist trade for countries outside the Empire. In other words, the British homeland, its autonomous territories, and various colonies form a single entity, while building high tariff barriers to prevent foreign goods from outside British territory from crossing the line. In order to determine and complete this policy, Australia, South Africa, India, and other places have implemented this policy one after another. The aforementioned increase in tariff rates and the abolition of commercial treaties with Japan are the results of implementing this group economy.

The implementation of British group economic nationalism directly dealt a fatal blow to the overseas invasion of Japanese goods.

IV

Since the implementation of the British nationalist economic group strategy, economic groups in European and American countries have also formed one after another, and it has now become a popular strategy in the world. Here is an introduction to the trend of these economic groups.

Portugal, from June 1, 1933, held a colonial conference, and on July 10, revised the decree for the purpose of unifying colonies, revising preferential tariffs between the country and its colonies, and establishing a colonial tariff committee to expand the protective tariffs of various colonies, and decided on the protection of navigation between colonies and its home country and the necessary facilities.

The three small countries of Lithuania, Latvia, and Estonia held a group economic conference and reached an agreement on tariffs and monetary policies.

Belgium, Italy, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and other countries that maintained the gold standard formed a gold standard group economy. The French Prime Minister also clearly stated in a speech on July 9 that the French economic group already had a considerable plan.

The United States, on July 7, notified its withdrawal from the "Treaty on the Abolition of Import and Export Prohibitions and Restrictions" established by the League of Nations in 1927; on July 12, it successively met with representatives from Argentina, Brazil, Colombia, Chile, and other South American countries to discuss closer trade relations and negotiate agreements. At the same time, it also expressed the opinion that tariffs on silk and other related items could be prepared for increase.

Recently, Germany has also felt that Japanese goods are not only invading their own country, but also gradually encroaching on their economic territory elsewhere. Recently, they have also been cooperating with European and American countries to prepare for an effective response to Japanese goods.

Looking at the facts listed above, countries around the world are rapidly forming economic groups in various forms. The occurrence of this phenomenon is, on the one hand, due to the failure of this World Economic Conference, which inevitably led to the strengthening of economic nationalism; but on the other hand, it must also be said to be a defensive movement due to the excessive activity of Japanese imperialist goods in overseas markets. Therefore, in the future, Japanese goods will not only be subjected to Britain's fierce resistance movement, which will deal a fatal blow from the front; but countries around the world will also adopt a defensive movement of encirclement and attack, so that Japanese goods can no longer be active in places of concern to various countries. This is an inevitable trend. Therefore, the impact on Japan after the economic grouping and the strengthening of economic nationalism in various countries can certainly be predicted.

V

What defensive strategies will Japan use against the movement to resist Japanese goods in various countries around the world? Naturally, the biggest enemy at present is Britain, so it initially used political means to establish the first act of the confrontation war against Britain.

The first act of this war is the issue of India's abolition of the commercial treaty and the increase in tariffs. At the time of the abolition of the treaty, it lodged strong protests, and used various methods through its ambassadors and consuls abroad to make direct and indirect negotiations. At the same time, yarn manufacturers agreed to not buy or sell Indian cotton as a retaliatory measure against Britain and India. Although the Indian and Japanese authorities are currently preparing to hold some kind of cooperation conference, this is foreseeable. While Britain and Japan are engaged in an economic confrontation war, this part of the cooperation agreement has no possibility of easing.

However, what general defensive measures will Japan take after being hit by the British economic group and the economic groups of various countries? Naturally, there is no other direction, and they will inevitably move towards the so-called Japanese-Manchu economic group or East Asian economic group that they are currently calling for. The northeastern provinces are already under the iron fist of Japanese imperialism, and they are using Chinese puppets to develop as much as possible all the information they can use for their activities and all means of exploitation. This piece of fat meat in China is naturally under the covetous gaze of Japanese imperialism, which will not be satisfied until it obtains it, while other imperialists are also actively preparing to become a target for contention.

However, specifically speaking of the so-called Japanese-Manchu economic group, if it progresses according to Japan's plan, it is actually directly colliding with the economic groups of various countries. Not only will the economic struggle between Britain and Japan, but also the economic struggle against the world, inevitably become deeper and more serious.

China's Foreign Trade and Domestic Trade 210

— Fa

At this year's annual meeting of the Chinese Economic Society, some people raised the issue of China's international trade and domestic trade, believing that there was no hope for the development of foreign trade, and that it would be better to improve domestic trade. A significant part of U.S. President Roosevelt's plan to revive American industry is also to protect and develop its domestic market. This is a question worth discussing, especially when international capitalism is working hard to go backwards.

Originally, foreign trade and domestic trade are not opposing terms, but rather the result of related economic development. In primitive times, there was no such thing as trade. Subsequently, the division of labor occurred between families, and then between clans and nations, and exchange relations occurred between them; until the form of the state, domestic trade occurred. The development of capitalism in the eighteenth century led to competition in foreign markets between countries. Not only did the international division of labor in production become a necessary condition for capitalism in various countries, but foreign markets also became the lifeline of each capitalist country. Therefore, international trade is only the progression or expansion of domestic trade that comes with economic development.

The reason why international trade has become the lifeline of capitalist countries is because of the development of industry. Developed industrial countries, on the one hand, need to promote the sales of their industrial products, and on the other hand, need to obtain raw materials, that is, they must develop international trade. Therefore, countries that have international trade relations with other countries can be divided into two categories: one is industrial countries, whose international trade is active, and can also be said to be aggressors; the other is agricultural countries with backward industries, whose entry into the vortex of international trade is forced, and can also be said to be invaded.

Unfortunately, China belongs to the latter category of countries in its international trade relations with other countries. China's closed-door barriers were initially opened by British cannons. In the early days of the intrusion of various countries' economic forces, the Chinese government and people had strong resistance, but they were finally assimilated in the torrent of international trade. Naturally, in international trade, the task that China fulfills is only to "absorb industrial manufactured goods and supply raw agricultural products." In this "unequal value" transaction, China has been exploited by the great powers.

But now, the situation has changed. The international market is becoming increasingly narrow, tariff wars between countries are intensifying, and Cunliffe even believes that world trade is "disappearing." Before the end of World War II and the clear division of the second world market, it is very obvious that although China wants to increase its obligation to "absorb manufactured goods and supply raw materials," it is also unable to do so.

Now, when there is no opportunity to develop foreign markets, countries are protecting their domestic markets. China's situation differs from other countries in two points, and these two characteristics make it more necessary and beneficial for China to protect and develop its domestic market.

First, China is mainly an agricultural country, and does not have industrial products that must seek foreign markets. The importance of its need for international trade is naturally less.

Second, China is a huge "import surplus country." If it can protect its domestic market and eliminate the dumping of foreign goods, this huge "import surplus" is enough for the market development of domestic industries.

Therefore, if it can eliminate foreign aggression, China's domestic trade is more important than foreign trade.

However, protecting and developing the domestic market also requires methods. Now, the "virgin land" of the four northeastern provinces, which has always been regarded as a great market for developing Chinese industry, is under the iron heels of the Japanese. It is reported that Yunnan is also in danger and may not escape being a sequel to the Northeast. Qingdao, an important commercial port in the central region, also has terrible rumors. In the situation where the land, which is one of the three essential elements of nation-building, cannot be guaranteed, it is difficult to protect the domestic market.

Securities: A Review of the Bond Market Last Week 212

=Initially Fell for Four Consecutive Days Due to Numerous Rumors=

=Continued with Short Covering, a Small Recovery=

Last week, from September 4th to 9th, the Hua Merchants Securities Market, after a full week, although it had resumed full-day four-session trading, the trend was still unremarkable. Daily fluctuations did not exceed half a yuan, making for a larger range of fluctuations. Generally, declines outweighed gains. Initially, the market price fell repeatedly due to the failure to quell the Min communists and the failure to reorganize the "96" bond. Subsequently, the Lushan Conference was quite successful, and a small recovery occurred. However, it is still not considered a transition to a rising trend, because there are many reforms after the Lushan Conference, and there are still many twists and turns in the future of market prices. On Monday, the market resumed full-day trading with two futures sessions each in the morning and afternoon, but trading was still light. Market prices continued to fluctuate, with only a difference of about 0.1 yuan between the morning and afternoon. From Tuesday to Thursday, one reason was that the Min rebellion was rampant, and people were timid. Another reason was that the reorganization of the "96" bond became a bubble again. Bulls gradually came out, and the Lushan Conference was just beginning, with different opinions still in the southwest. Therefore, the market showed an oversupply every day. Although large households had entries and exits, they ultimately sold more than they bought, and the price fell by 0.3-0.4 yuan to about 0.5 yuan every day. On Friday and Saturday, the Lushan Conference concluded successfully, and the market rose slightly due to short covering. The two days collectively rose by 0.1-0.2 yuan to 0.5-0.6 yuan. The trend is still weak, and there are many waves in the future. As a result of the weekly market prices, the average decline was 0.1-0.2 yuan to 0.45 yuan. However, the "96" bond has fallen by more than 1 yuan. The total transaction volume was 43,686,000 yuan.

Silk and Tea: Imports of Rayon are Becoming Smoother 214

(Shaoxing Autumn Cocoon Prices Rise) This year's autumn cocoons in the four villages of Shaoxing are abundant and of good quality. Cocoon merchants are vying to purchase them. Farmers believe that autumn leaf prices are high this year and the cost of silkworms is higher, so they are willing to sell them at high prices. Therefore, although the goods arriving in the market recently are still not weak, the price of cocoons is expected to rise. The price of good cocoons has opened at 45-46 yuan.

(New York Raw Silk Consumption Decreases Significantly) In the middle of last month, strikes in New York silk factories occurred frequently, and the consumption of raw silk decreased significantly. The total consumption of silk for the whole month was only 42,852 bales, a sharp decrease of nearly 17,000 bales compared to the same month last year.

(Imports of Rayon Exceed 1,000 Cases) Last week, the Italian postal ship Count of Savoy loaded 1,084 cases, which were stored in customs warehouses.

Sugar Market: Chinese Refined Sugar Calls for a Price Increase of Half a 角 215

Yesterday, the sugar market saw limited activity. The Public Association's pricing trend was flat. Grade 24 coarse granulated white sugar was priced at 21 yuan and 6.5 角, up 7 分 from the previous (8th) day, with only 50 bags traded. Dutch Red PK mark and MKGA mark both fell by 1 角 from 16 yuan and 6.5 角. Taikoo Sugar B mark was priced at 21 yuan and 8 角, with some transactions. Chinese Guohua refined white sugar wanted to raise the price by 1.5 角, with Grade 1 called for 20 yuan and 7.5 角, but no transaction was made. Chaozhou Qing opened with dozens of bags of Gao Huanggang Qing at 15 yuan and 7.5 角.

Grains: Du Japonica Rice Levels Out, Metavariant Continues to Weaken 216

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were over 30 sources. Both retail and wholesale sales were slightly better than before, with a total of 1,600 to 1,700 bags of Yantai rice passing through. Therefore, the situation slightly improved, but ultimately, due to flat consumer sentiment, the market remained stable. Therefore, there were no significant changes in the prices of various types of thick japonica, thin rice, Du Yangjian, and Xin Jian. The price of metavariant remained weak and fell by several 角. He Xia's new japonica rice turned flat, and Changdong's new rice also remained stable.

Talk

On Selfishness Qian Xu 217

Some people say, "China is bound to perish." Others say, "If China doesn't perish, there's no justice in the world." Although the wording differs, their prediction of China's inevitable demise is the same. The reasons these "prophets" give for China's demise are nothing more than the habits—or rather, the deeply ingrained flaws—of the Chinese people: a tendency towards selfishness and self-interest, a rush to be first, individualism, an inability to think about the big picture, shortsightedness, and so on. These "prophets," observing these phenomena, which are almost universal, feel pessimistic and sigh loudly. In their pessimism and lamentation, they even start to "assimilate," walking down the path of selfishness, rushing to be first, individualism... and deeply feel that old China is beyond redemption.

Indeed, the Chinese are a bit selfish... At train stations, tram stops, post offices, banks, and various public places, who doesn't want to be the first to buy a ticket and get on the vehicle? Who doesn't want to be the first to get their business done? Even in cinemas or classrooms without assigned seats in a school, who doesn't rush in to occupy the best seat? Focusing on personal comfort, they naturally can't consider the convenience of others. Under these circumstances, our "prophets" also realize that being too "foolish" isn't the way to go, so they cleverly, instinctively, and bravely become just as "selfish." Their reason for "assimilation" is, "Everyone else is doing it, why should I be a fool?" At the same time, they lament "the decline of morality" to show that they didn't originally want to be "like this," but are merely "imitating."

However, the Chinese people's deep-seated flaws don't stop there. Even after the loss of the four northeastern provinces, the people in Shanghai continue to sing, dance, and indulge in extravagance, as if nothing has happened. The sound of cannons can't awaken them from their dreams of getting rich, and hot blood can't excite their numbed minds! Even now, many people are still dreaming of making a fortune of 500,000 yuan! Our "prophets" may unfortunately be proven right!

Will China really perish? Based on an organization built on "selfishness," China will indeed perish.

How can we become "unselfish"? It can only start with oneself. If you wait until others are unselfish before you become unselfish, it will never happen. Only when everyone can eliminate the concept of "selfishness" will there be no more problems. There will be no need to chant high-sounding slogans of struggle and sacrifice. However, there may be so-called "clever people" who laugh, laughing at you all as "fools." However, in these times, what is needed are precisely "fools"—utter fools who can shoulder great responsibilities. "Clever people" should only be given the punishment of "exile."

Economics and Power 人 218

I believe that no matter what you want to accomplish, if you don't have "economics," you can't do anything.

At a school's administrative meeting, an incident occurred involving a conflict between "economics" and "power." The school's finances are not considered wealthy, because it is still in a period of struggle and effort, which I should first explain. Near the end of the meeting, a Dean of Students suggested to the Principal that a fixed portion of the budget be allocated as office expenses for the Dean of Students Office. The reason was, "You can't achieve results without money; if you have no control over the budget, then even if you plan the entire strategy, it will be a waste of effort and never be implemented. If you just muddle through and treat it as an empty formality, you can't justify your responsibility." The Principal's response was as follows: "Because our school is still newly established, it's natural that we aren't financially abundant. Although the office expenses for each 'department' should be clearly allocated, under our current circumstances, everyone should consider the facts and understand together. Because we want to make every effort to push the school forward, if there is something the Dean of Students Office needs to do that the school can afford, then we can just do it. If we think it's necessary but the school's finances make it impossible, then we'll put it on hold for now."
